}






function
google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Billy_Joel';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"billy,joel,_,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>William
Martin</b>
&quot;<b>Billy</b>&quot;
<b>Joel</b>
(born
May
9,
1949)
is
an
<a
href="/wiki/United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States">American</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Pianist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pianist">pianist</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Singer-songwriter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Singer-songwriter">singer-songwriter</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Composer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Composer">composer</a>.
Since
releasing
his
first
hit
song,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Piano_Man_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piano
Man
(song)">Piano
Man</a>,&quot;
in
1973,
Joel
has
become
the
sixth
best
selling
recording
artist
and
the
third-best-selling
solo
artist
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
compilation
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Billy_Joel_albums)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
Hits
(Billy
Joel
albums)">Greatest
Hits
Vol.
1
&amp;
2</a></i>
is
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_the_United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
albums
in
the
United
States">third-best-selling
album
in
the
United
States
by
discs
shipped</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA-2_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-2-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Joel
had
Top
40
hits
in
the
1970s,
1980s,
and
1990s,
achieving
33
Top
40
hits
in
the
United
States,
all
of
which
he
wrote
himself.
He
is
also
a
six-time
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
winner
who
has
been
nominated
for
23
Grammy
Awards
throughout
his
career.
He
has
sold
over
150
million
records
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Joel
was
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame">Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame</a>
(1992),
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
(1999),
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Long_Island_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
Island
Music
Hall
of
Fame">Long
Island
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
(2006).
In
2001,
Joel
received
the
Johnny
Mercer
Award
from
the
Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame.
In
2013,
Joel
received
the
Kennedy
Center
Honors,
the
nation's
highest
honor
for
influencing
American
culture
through
the
arts.
With
the
exception
of
the
2007
songs
&quot;All
My
Life&quot;
and
&quot;Christmas
in
Fallujah,&quot;
Joel
stopped
writing
and
releasing
pop/rock
material
after
1993's
<i><a
href="/wiki/River_of_Dreams?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="River
of
Dreams">River
of
Dreams</a></i>.
However,
he
continues
to
tour,
and
he
plays
songs
from
all
eras
of
his
solo
career
in
his
concerts.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Joel
was
born
in
<a
href="/wiki/The_Bronx?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Bronx">the
Bronx</a>
on
May
9,
1949<sup
id="cite_ref-bio_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bio-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
raised
in
the
suburb
of
<a
href="/wiki/Hicksville,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hicksville,
New
York">Hicksville,
New
York</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-htt_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-htt-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
father,
Howard
(born
Helmuth),
was
born
in
Germany,
the
son
of
German
merchant
and
manufacturer
<a
href="/wiki/Karl_Amson_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Karl
Amson
Joel">Karl
Amson
Joel</a>.
Howard
emigrated
to
Switzerland
and
later
to
the
United
States
(via
Cuba,
as
immigration
quotas
for
German
Jews
prevented
direct
immigration
at
the
time)
in
order
to
escape
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nazi
Germany">Nazi
regime</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-htt_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-htt-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Billy
Joel's
mother,
Rosalind
Nyman,
was
born
in
England
to
Philip
and
Rebecca
Nyman.
Both
of
Joel's
parents
were
<a
href="/wiki/Jew?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jew"
class="mw-redirect">Jewish</a>.
They
divorced
in
1960,
and
his
father
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/Vienna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vienna">Vienna</a>,
Austria.
Billy
has
a
sister,
Judith
Joel,
and
a
half-brother,
<a
href="/wiki/Alexander_Joel_(conductor)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alexander
Joel
(conductor)">Alexander
Joel</a>,
an
acclaimed
classical
conductor
in
Europe
who
is
currently
chief
musical
director
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Braunschweig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Staatstheater
Braunschweig">Staatstheater
Braunschweig</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Villager_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Villager-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Joel's
father
was
a
classical
pianist.
Billy
reluctantly
began
piano
lessons
at
an
early
age,
at
his
mother's
insistence,
his
teachers
including
the
noted
American
pianist
<a
href="/wiki/Morton_Estrin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Morton
Estrin">Morton
Estrin</a><sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Timothy_Ford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Timothy
Ford">Timothy
Ford</a>;
he
was
bullied
because
of
his
interest
in
music
rather
than
sports.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(October
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
As
a
teenager,
Joel
took
up
<a
href="/wiki/Boxing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boxing">boxing</a>
so
that
he
would
be
able
to
defend
himself.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(October
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
He
boxed
successfully
on
the
amateur
<a
href="/wiki/Golden_Gloves?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Golden
Gloves">Golden
Gloves</a>
circuit
for
a
short
time,
winning
twenty-two
bouts,
but
abandoned
the
sport
shortly
after
his
nose
was
broken
in
his
twenty-fourth
boxing
match.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Joel
attended
Hicksville
High
School
in
1967,
but
he
did
not
graduate
with
his
class.
He
had
been
playing
at
a
piano
bar
to
help
his
mother
make
ends
meet,
which
interfered
with
his
attendance:<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
at
the
end
of
his
senior
year,
Joel
did
not
have
enough
credits
to
graduate.
Rather
than
attend
summer
school
to
earn
his
diploma,
Joel
decided
to
begin
a
career
in
music:
&quot;I
told
them,
'To
hell
with
it.
If
I'm
not
going
to
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
University">Columbia
University</a>,
I'm
going
to
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>,
and
you
don't
need
a
high
school
diploma
over
there'.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joel
did,
in
fact,
eventually
sign
with
Columbia.
In
1992,
he
submitted
essays
to
the
school
board
and
was
awarded
his
diploma
at
Hicksville
High's
annual
graduation
ceremony,
25
years
after
leaving.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_career">Music
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Music
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_career">Early
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Early
career">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>After
seeing
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Ed
Sullivan
Show">The
Ed
Sullivan
Show</a></i>,
Joel
decided
to
pursue
a
career
in
music.
In
an
interview
he
said
of
the
group's
impact,
&quot;That
one
performance
changed
my
life
...
Up
to
that
moment
I'd
never
considered
playing
rock
as
a
career.
And
when
I
saw
four
guys
who
didn't
look
like
they'd
come
out
of
the
Hollywood
star
mill,
who
played
their
own
songs
and
instruments,
and
especially
because
you
could
see
this
look
in
John
Lennon's
face
--
and
he
looked
like
he
was
always
saying:
'F---
you!'
--
I
said:
'I
know
these
guys,
I
can
relate
to
these
guys,
I
am
these
guys.'
This
is
what
I'm
going
to
do
--
play
in
a
rock
band'.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Joel
founded
the
Echoes,
a
group
that
specialized
in
<a
href="/wiki/British_Invasion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="British
Invasion">British
Invasion</a>
covers.
When
the
Echoes
became
popular
in
New
York,
Joel
left
high
school
to
become
a
professional
musician.<sup
id="cite_ref-sing365_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sing365-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
Echoes
began
recording
in
1965;
Billy
Joel
was
originally
hired
by
Snuff
Garret
as
a
pianist
for
Bobby
Vee,
however
he
was
fired
before
doing
any
records
or
shows
because
he
refused
to
wear
the
matching
jackets
the
band
was
to
wear
.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(November
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
Billy
Joel
(then
16)
also
played
piano
on
several
records
released
through
<a
href="/wiki/Kama_Sutra_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kama
Sutra
Records">Kama
Sutra
Productions</a>
and
on
recordings
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Shadow_Morton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shadow
Morton">Shadow
Morton</a>.
Joel
played
on
a
<a
href="/wiki/Demo_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Demo
(music)">demo</a>
version
of
<a
href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Pack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leader
of
the
Pack">Leader
of
the
Pack</a>,
which
would
become
a
major
hit
for
<a
href="/wiki/The_Shangri-Las?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Shangri-Las">the
Shangri-Las</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright"
style="width:
212px;">









<div
class="thumbinner">










<div
style="margin:
1px;
width:
202px">











<div
class="thumbimage">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Hassles.png"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/The_Hassles.png/200px-The_Hassles.png"
width="200"
height="144"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/The_Hassles.png/300px-The_Hassles.png
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/d/df/The_Hassles.png
2x"
/></a>










</div>











<div
class="thumbcaption"
style="clear:left">











Billy
Joel
(left)
with












<a
href="/wiki/The_Hassles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Hassles">The
Hassles</a>.










</div>










</div>










<div
style="margin:
1px;
width:
202px">











<div
class="thumbimage">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Attila_in_1970.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/02/Attila_in_1970.jpg/200px-Attila_in_1970.jpg"
width="200"
height="162"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/02/Attila_in_1970.jpg/300px-Attila_in_1970.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/02/Attila_in_1970.jpg/400px-Attila_in_1970.jpg
2x"
/></a>










</div>











<div
class="thumbcaption"
style="clear:left">











Billy
Joel
(left)
and
Jon
Small
(right),












<a
href="/wiki/Attila_(rock_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Attila
(rock
band)">Attila</a>,
in
1970.










</div>










</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
late
1965,
the
Echoes
changed
their
name
to
the
Emeralds
and
then
to
the
Lost
Souls.
Joel
left
the
band
in
1967
to
join
<a
href="/wiki/The_Hassles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Hassles">the
Hassles</a>,
a
Long
Island
group
that
had
signed
with
<a
href="/wiki/United_Artists_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
Artists
Records">United
Artists
Records</a>.
Over
the
next
year
and
a
half
they
released
four
singles
and
two
albums
(<i>The
Hassles</i>
and
<i>Hour
of
the
Wolf</i>).
All
were
commercial
failures.
Joel
and
drummer
Jon
Small
left
the
Hassles
in
1969
to
form
the
duo
<a
href="/wiki/Attila_(rock_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Attila
(rock
band)">Attila</a>,
releasing
an
<a
href="/wiki/Eponymous?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eponymous"
class="mw-redirect">eponymous</a>
debut
album
in
July
1970.
The
duo
disbanded
the
following
October
when
Joel
began
an
affair
with
Small's
wife,
Elizabeth,
whom
Joel
eventually
married.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Cold_Spring_Harbor"><i>Cold
Spring
Harbor</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Cold
Spring
Harbor">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Joel
signed
a
contract
with
the
record
company
Family
Productions
(owned
by
Artie
Ripp),
with
which
he
recorded
his
first
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cold_Spring_Harbor_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cold
Spring
Harbor
(album)">Cold
Spring
Harbor</a></i>
(a
reference
to
<a
href="/wiki/Cold_Spring_Harbor,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cold
Spring
Harbor,
New
York">Cold
Spring
Harbor,
New
York</a>,
a
town
on
<a
href="/wiki/Long_Island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
Island">Long
Island</a>).
Released
in
1971,
the
album
was
a
technical
and
commercial
disappointment.
Ripp
mastered
the
album
incorrectly,
distorting
Joel's
vocals;
Joel
soon
grew
frustrated
with
Ripp's
incompetence
and
with
the
onerous
terms
of
their
contract.</p>








<p>The
popular
songs
&quot;She's
Got
a
Way&quot;
and
&quot;Everybody
Loves
You
Now&quot;
were
originally
released
on
this
album
but
went
largely
unnoticed
until
being
released
as
live
performances
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Songs_in_the_Attic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songs
in
the
Attic">Songs
in
the
Attic</a></i>
(1981).
They
have
since
become
popular
in
concert.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(October
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
Columbia
released
a
remastered
version
of
<i>Cold
Spring
Harbor</i>
in
1984,
which
reached
#158
in
the
US
and
#95
in
the
UK.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(October
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>








<p>After
performing
locally
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>
in
the
fall
of
1971,
Joel
moved
to
Los
Angeles
in
early
1972
to
escape
his
unfavorable
contract,
adopting
the
stage
name
&quot;Bill
Martin.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
six
months
he
worked
at
The
Executive
Room
<a
href="/wiki/Piano_bar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piano
bar">piano
bar</a>
on
<a
href="/wiki/Wilshire_Boulevard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wilshire
Boulevard">Wilshire
Boulevard</a>,
composing
his
signature
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Piano_Man_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piano
Man
(song)">Piano
Man</a>&quot;
about
the
bar's
patrons.
That
year
Joel
toured
with
his
band
(<a
href="/wiki/Rhys_Clark?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rhys
Clark">Rhys
Clark</a>
on
drums,
Al
Hertzberg
on
guitar,
and
Larry
Russell
on
bass)
throughout
the
United
States
and
Puerto
Rico,
opening
for
groups
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/J._Geils_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J.
Geils
Band"
class="mw-redirect">J.
Geils
Band</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beach
Boys">The
Beach
Boys</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taj
Mahal
(musician)">Taj
Mahal</a>.
Joel's
performance
at
the
Puerto
Rican
<a
href="/wiki/Mar_y_sol_festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mar
y
sol
festival"
class="mw-redirect">Mar
y
sol
festival</a>
was
especially
well-received:
interest
in
his
music
grew.<sup
id="cite_ref-unauthorized_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unauthorized-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
<a
href="/wiki/Philadelphia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>,
the
radio
station
<a
href="/wiki/WMMR?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="WMMR">WMMR</a>-FM
began
playing
a
<a
href="/wiki/Live_concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
concert"
class="mw-redirect">concert</a>
recording
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Captain_Jack_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Captain
Jack
(Billy
Joel
song)">Captain
Jack</a>&quot;,
which
became
an
underground
hit
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="East
Coast
of
the
United
States">East
Coast</a>.
Herb
Gordon,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>
executive,
heard
Joel's
music
and
introduced
him
to
the
company.
Joel
signed
a
recording
contract
with
Columbia
in
1972
and
moved
to
Los
Angeles,
where
he
lived
for
three
years
(time
that
he
now
regrets).<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_Columbia_years:_1973.E2.80.931976">Early
Columbia
years:
1973–1976</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Early
Columbia
years:
1973–1976">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TheEntertainer-Billy.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""

http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/a/a7/TheEntertainer-Billy.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TheEntertainer-Billy.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"

/></a>










</div>
Billy
Joel
on
the
cover
of
the
single
for
&quot;The
Entertainer&quot;
(1975).









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Despite
Joel's
new
contract,
he
was
still
legally
bound
to
Family
Productions.
Ripp
sold
Joel's
first
contract
to
Columbia
on
the
conditions
that
the
Family
Productions
logo
be
displayed
alongside
the
Columbia
logo
on
Joel's
next
ten
albums
and
that
Ripp
be
paid
a
royalty
on
every
record
sold.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(October
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Walter_Yetnikoff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walter
Yetnikoff">Walter
Yetnikoff</a>,
the
president
of
CBS/Columbia
Records
at
the
time,
bought
back
the
rights
to
Joel's
songs
in
the
late
1970s,
giving
the
rights
to
Joel
as
a
birthday
gift.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
Yetnikoff
notes
in
the
documentary
film
<i>The
Last
Play
at
Shea</i>
that
he
had
to
threaten
Ripp
to
close
the
deal.</p>








<p>Joel's
first
album
with
Columbia
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/Piano_Man_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piano
Man
(album)">Piano
Man</a></i>,
released
in
1973.
Despite
modest
sales,
<i>Piano
Man</i>'s
title
track
became
his
signature
song,
ending
nearly
every
concert.
That
year
Joel's
touring
band
changed.
Guitarist
Al
Hertzberg
was
replaced
by
Don
Evans,
and
bassist
Larry
Russell
by
Patrick
McDonald,
himself
replaced
in
late
1974
by
<a
href="/wiki/Doug_Stegmeyer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doug
Stegmeyer">Doug
Stegmeyer</a>,
who
would
stay
with
Joel
until
1989.
Rhys
Clark
returned
as
drummer
and
Tom
Whitehorse
as
banjoist
and
pedal
steel
player;
Johnny
Almond
joined
as
saxophonist
and
keyboardist.
The
band
toured
the
US
and
Canada
extensively,
appearing
on
popular
music
shows.
Joel's
songwriting
began
attracting
more
attention;
in
1974
<a
href="/wiki/Helen_Reddy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Helen
Reddy">Helen
Reddy</a>
recorded
&quot;You're
My
Home&quot;
(<i>Piano
Man</i>).</p>








<p>Joel
recorded
a
second
album
in
Los
Angeles:
<i><a
href="/wiki/Streetlife_Serenade?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Streetlife
Serenade">Streetlife
Serenade</a></i>.
His
manager
was
Jon
Troy,
an
old
friend
from
the
New
York
neighborhood
of
<a
href="/wiki/Bedford-Stuyvesant?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bedford-Stuyvesant"
class="mw-redirect">Bedford-Stuyvesant</a>.
Troy
would
soon
be
replaced
by
Joel's
wife
Elizabeth.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Streetlife
Serenade</i>
contains
references
to
<a
href="/wiki/Suburbia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suburbia"
class="mw-redirect">suburbia</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Inner_city?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Inner
city">inner
city</a>.
It
is
perhaps
best
known
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Entertainer_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Entertainer
(song)">The
Entertainer</a>&quot;,
a
#34
hit
in
the
United
States.
Upset
that
&quot;Piano
Man&quot;
had
been
significantly
cut
for
radio
play,
Joel
wrote
&quot;The
Entertainer&quot;
as
a
sarcastic
response:
&quot;If
you're
gonna
have
a
hit,
you
gotta
make
it
fit,
so
they
cut
it
down
to
3:05.&quot;
Although
<i>Streetlife
Serenade</i>
is
often
considered
one
of
Joel's
weaker
albums
(Joel
dislikes
it
himself),
it
contains
the
notable
songs
&quot;Los
Angelenos&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Root_Beer_Rag?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Root
Beer
Rag">Root
Beer
Rag</a>&quot;,
an
<a
href="/wiki/Instrumental?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Instrumental">instrumental</a>
that
was
a
staple
of
his
live
set
in
the
1970s.</p>








<p>In
late
1975,
he
played
piano
and
organ
on
several
tracks
on
<a
href="/wiki/Bo_Diddley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bo
Diddley">Bo
Diddley</a>'s
<i>The
20th
Anniversary
of
Rock
'n'
Roll</i>
all-star
album.</p>








<p>Disenchanted
with
L.A.,
Joel
returned
to
New
York
in
1976
and
recorded
<i><a
href="/wiki/Turnstiles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Turnstiles">Turnstiles</a></i>,
the
first
album
he
recorded
with
the
group
of
hand-picked
musicians
who
became
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Joel_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Joel
Band">Billy
Joel
Band</a>.
Produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/James_William_Guercio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
William
Guercio">James
William
Guercio</a>
(then
<a
href="/wiki/Chicago_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chicago
(band)">Chicago</a>'s
producer),
<i>Turnstiles</i>
was
first
recorded
at
Caribou
Ranch
with
members
of
<a
href="/wiki/Elton_John?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elton
John">Elton
John</a>'s
band.
Dissatisfied
with
the
result,
Joel
re-recorded
the
songs
and
produced
the
album
himself.</p>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Say_Goodbye_to_Hollywood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Say
Goodbye
to
Hollywood">Say
Goodbye
to
Hollywood</a>&quot;
was
a
minor
hit;
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_Spector?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
Spector">Ronnie
Spector</a>
recorded
a
cover
as
did
<a
href="/wiki/Nigel_Olsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nigel
Olsson">Nigel
Olsson</a>,
then
drummer
with
Elton
John.
(In
a
2008
radio
interview,
Joel
said
that
he
no
longer
performs
the
song
because
singing
it
in
its
high
original
key
&quot;shreds&quot;
his
<a
href="/wiki/Vocal_folds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vocal
folds">vocal
cords</a>.)
Though
never
released
as
a
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/New_York_State_of_Mind?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
State
of
Mind">New
York
State
of
Mind</a>&quot;
became
one
of
Joel's
best-known
songs;
<a
href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barbra
Streisand">Barbra
Streisand</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Bennett">Tony
Bennett</a>
have
each
recorded
covers
(Bennet's
a
duet
with
Joel
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Playing_with_My_Friends:_Bennett_Sings_the_Blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Playing
with
My
Friends:
Bennett
Sings
the
Blues"
class="mw-redirect">Playing
with
My
Friends:
Bennett
Sings
the
Blues</a></i>).
Other
notable
songs
from
the
album
include
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Summer,_Highland_Falls?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Summer,
Highland
Falls"
class="mw-redirect">Summer,
Highland
Falls</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Miami_2017_(Seen_the_Lights_Go_Out_on_Broadway)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miami
2017
(Seen
the
Lights
Go
Out
on
Broadway)">Miami
2017
(Seen
the
Lights
Go
Out
on
Broadway)</a>&quot;,
&quot;Say
Goodbye
to
Hollywood&quot;,
(a
live
version
of
which
became
a
Top
40
hit),
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Prelude/Angry_Young_Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prelude/Angry
Young
Man">Prelude/Angry
Young
Man</a>&quot;,
a
concert
mainstay.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Stranger_and_52nd_Street"><i>The
Stranger</i>
and
<i>52nd
Street</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"

section:

Stranger
and
52nd
Street">edit</a>]</span></h3>

<div

<a

</div>
Billy
Joel
on
the
cover
of
the
single
for
&quot;Only
The
Good
Die
Young,&quot;
1977.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Columbia
Records
introduced
Joel
to
<a
href="/wiki/Phil_Ramone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Ramone">Phil
Ramone</a>,
who
would
produce
all
of
Joel's
studio
albums
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Stranger_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Stranger
(album)">The
Stranger</a></i>
(1977)
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Bridge_(Billy_Joel_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Bridge
(Billy
Joel
album)">The
Bridge</a></i>
(1986).
<i>The
Stranger</i>
was
an
enormous
commercial
success,
yielding
four
Top-25
hits
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
charts:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Just_the_Way_You_Are_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Just
the
Way
You
Are
(Billy
Joel
song)">Just
the
Way
You
Are</a>&quot;
(#3),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Movin%27_Out_(Anthony%27s_Song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Movin'
Out
(Anthony's
Song)">Movin'
Out
(Anthony's
Song)</a>&quot;
(#17),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Only_the_Good_Die_Young?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Only
the
Good
Die
Young">Only
the
Good
Die
Young</a>&quot;
(#24),
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She%27s_Always_a_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She's
Always
a
Woman">She's
Always
a
Woman</a>&quot;
(#17).
Joel's
first
Top
Ten
album,
<i>The
Stranger</i>
was
certified
multi-platinum
and
reached
number
two
on
the
charts,
outselling
<a
href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Garfunkel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Simon
&amp;
Garfunkel">Simon
&amp;
Garfunkel</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bridge_Over_Troubled_Water?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bridge
Over
Troubled
Water"
class="mw-redirect">Bridge
Over
Troubled
Water</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
Columbia's
previous
best-selling
album.
<i>The
Stranger</i>
also
featured
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Scenes_from_an_Italian_Restaurant?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scenes
from
an
Italian
Restaurant">Scenes
from
an
Italian
Restaurant</a>&quot;,
an
<a
href="/wiki/Album-oriented_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Album-oriented
rock">album-oriented
rock</a>
classic,
which
has
become
one
of
his
best-known
songs.</p>








<p><i>The
Stranger</i>
won
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy</a>
awards
for
<a
href="/wiki/Record_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
of
the
Year"
class="mw-redirect">Record
of
the
Year</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Song
of
the
Year">Song
of
the
Year</a>
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Just_the_Way_You_Are_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Just
the
Way
You
Are
(Billy
Joel
song)">Just
the
Way
You
Are</a>&quot;—written
for
Joel's
first
wife,
Elizabeth
Weber).
On
tour
in
<a
href="/wiki/Paris?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paris">Paris</a>,
Joel
learned
the
news
late
at
night
in
his
hotel
room.<sup
id="cite_ref-sing365_16-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sing365-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
ranked
<i>The
Stranger</i>
the
70th
greatest
album
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Expectations
were
high
for
Joel's
next
album,
<a
href="/wiki/52nd_Street_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="52nd
Street
(album)"><i>52nd
Street</i></a>,
which
he
released
in
1978,
naming
it
after
Manhattan's
famous
<a
href="/wiki/52nd_Street_(Manhattan)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="52nd
Street
(Manhattan)">52nd
Street</a>.
The
album
sold
over
seven
million
copies,
propelled
to
number
one
on
the
charts
by
the
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/My_Life_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Life
(Billy
Joel
song)">My
Life</a>&quot;
(#3),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Big_Shot_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Shot
(song)">Big
Shot</a>&quot;
(#14),
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Honesty_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honesty
(Billy
Joel
song)">Honesty</a>&quot;
(#24).
&quot;My
Life&quot;
became
the
theme
song
for
a
new
television
sitcom,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bosom_Buddies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bosom
Buddies">Bosom
Buddies</a></i>,
which
featured
actor
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Hanks">Tom
Hanks</a>
in
one
of
his
earliest
roles.
<i>52nd
Street</i>
won
Grammy
awards
for
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Pop_Vocal_Performance,_Male?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Pop
Vocal
Performance,
Male"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Pop
Vocal
Performance,
Male</a>
and
Album
of
the
Year.
It
was
the
first
album
to
be
released
on
compact
disc,
going
on
sale
alongside
Sony's
CD
player
CDP-101
on
October
1,
1982.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1979,
Joel
also
traveled
to
<a
href="/wiki/Havana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Havana">Havana</a>,
Cuba,
to
participate
in
the
historic
<a
href="/wiki/Havana_Jam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Havana
Jam">Havana
Jam</a>
festival
that
took
place
between
March
2–4,
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Rita_Coolidge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rita
Coolidge">Rita
Coolidge</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kris
Kristofferson">Kris
Kristofferson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Stills">Stephen
Stills</a>,
the
CBS
Jazz
All-Stars,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Trio_of_Doom?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trio
of
Doom">Trio
of
Doom</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Fania_All-Stars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fania
All-Stars">Fania
All-Stars</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Swan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Swan">Billy
Swan</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bramlett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bonnie
Bramlett">Bonnie
Bramlett</a>,
Mike
Finnegan,
<a
href="/wiki/Weather_Report?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Weather
Report">Weather
Report</a>,
and
an
array
of
Cuban
artists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Irakere?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Irakere">Irakere</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Pacho_Alonso?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pacho
Alonso">Pacho
Alonso</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Tata_G%C3%BCines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tata
G&uuml;ines">Tata
G&uuml;ines</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Orquesta_Arag%C3%B3n?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Orquesta
Arag&oacute;n">Orquesta
Arag&oacute;n</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
performance
is
captured
in
<a
href="/wiki/Ernesto_Juan_Castellanos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ernesto
Juan
Castellanos">Ernesto
Juan
Castellanos</a>'s
documentary
<i><a
href="/wiki/Havana_Jam_%2779?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Havana
Jam
'79">Havana
Jam
'79</a></i>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_1980s">Early
1980s</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Early
1980s">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>The
success
of
his
piano-driven
ballads
like
&quot;Just
the
Way
You
Are&quot;,
&quot;She's
Always
a
Woman&quot;,
and
&quot;Honesty&quot;
led
some
critics
to
label
Joel
a
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Ballad?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ballad">balladeer</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Soft_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soft
rock">soft
rocker</a>&quot;.
Joel
thought
these
labels
were
unfair
and
insulting,
and
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Glass_Houses?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glass
Houses">Glass
Houses</a></i>,
he
tried
to
record
an
album
that
proved
that
he
could
rock
harder
than
his
critics
gave
him
credit
for,
occasionally
imitating
and
referencing
the
style
of
<a
href="/wiki/New_Wave_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Wave
music"
class="mw-redirect">New
Wave</a>
rock
music
that
was
starting
to
become
popular
at
the
time.
On
the
front
cover
of
the
album,
Joel
is
pictured
in
a
leather
jacket,
about
to
throw
a
rock
at
a
glass
house
(referencing
the
adage
that
&quot;people
who
live
in
glass
houses
shouldn't
throw
stones&quot;).</p>








<p><i>Glass
Houses</i>
spent
6
weeks
at
#1
on
the
Billboard
chart
and
yielded
such
hits
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_May_Be_Right_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
May
Be
Right
(song)">You
May
Be
Right</a>&quot;
(used
as
the
theme
song,
covered
by
<a
href="/wiki/Southside_Johnny?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Southside
Johnny">Southside
Johnny</a>,
for
the
CBS
mid-1990s
sitcom
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dave%27s_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave's
World">Dave's
World</a></i>)
(#7,
May
1980),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Don%27t_Ask_Me_Why_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don't
Ask
Me
Why
(Billy
Joel
song)">Don't
Ask
Me
Why</a>&quot;
(#19,
September
1980),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sometimes_a_Fantasy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sometimes
a
Fantasy">Sometimes
a
Fantasy</a>&quot;
(#36,
November
1980)
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It%27s_Still_Rock_and_Roll_to_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It's
Still
Rock
and
Roll
to
Me">It's
Still
Rock
and
Roll
to
Me</a>&quot;,
which
became
Joel's
first
Billboard
#1
song
(for
two
weeks)
in
July
1980.
&quot;It's
Still
Rock
and
Roll
to
Me&quot;
spent
11
weeks
in
the
top
10
of
the
Billboard
Hot
100
and
was
the
7th
biggest
hit
of
1980
according
to
American
Top
40.</p>








<p><i>Glass
Houses</i>
won
the
Grammy
for
Best
Rock
Vocal
Performance,
Male.
It
would
also
win
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Award">American
Music
Award</a>
for
Favorite
Album,
Pop/Rock
category.
The
album's
closing
song,
&quot;Through
The
Long
Night&quot;
(<a
href="/wiki/B-side?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B-side"
class="mw-redirect">B-side</a>
of
the
&quot;It's
Still
Rock
&amp;
Roll
to
Me&quot;
single),
was
a
lullaby
that
featured
Joel
harmonizing
with
himself
in
a
song
he
says
was
inspired
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>'
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Yes_It_Is?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yes
It
Is">Yes
It
Is</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-unauthorized_20-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unauthorized-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>His
next
release,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Songs_in_the_Attic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songs
in
the
Attic">Songs
in
the
Attic</a></i>,
was
composed
of
live
performances
of
less
well-known
songs
from
the
beginning
of
his
career.
It
was
recorded
during
larger
US
arenas
and
intimate
night
club
shows
in
June
and
July
1980.
This
release
introduced
many
fans,
who
discovered
Joel
when
<i>The
Stranger</i>
became
a
smash
in
1977,
to
many
of
his
earlier
compositions.
The
album
reached
#8
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
chart
and
produced
two
hit
singles:
&quot;Say
Goodbye
to
Hollywood&quot;
(#17),
and
&quot;She's
Got
a
Way&quot;
(#23).
It
sold
over
3&nbsp;million
copies.
Though
not
as
successful
as
some
of
his
previous
albums,
the
album
was
still
considered
a
success
by
Joel.<sup
id="cite_ref-unauthorized_20-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unauthorized-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
next
wave
of
Joel's
career
commenced
with
the
recording
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Nylon_Curtain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Nylon
Curtain">The
Nylon
Curtain</a></i>.
With
<i>The
Nylon
Curtain</i>,
Joel
became
more
ambitious
with
his
songwriting,
trying
his
hand
at
writing
topical
songs
like
&quot;Allentown&quot;
and
&quot;Goodnight
Saigon&quot;.
Joel
has
stated
that
he
wanted
the
album
to
communicate
his
feelings
about
the
American
dream
and
how
changes
in
American
politics
during
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronald
Reagan">Reagan
years</a>
meant
that
&quot;all
of
a
sudden
you
weren't
going
to
be
able
to
inherit
[the
kind
of
life]
your
old
man
had.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-ncvideo_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ncvideo-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
tried
to
be
more
ambitious
in
his
use
of
the
recording
studio.
Joel
said
that
he
wanted
to
&quot;create
a
sonic
masterpiece&quot;
on
<i>The
Nylon
Curtain</i>.
So
he
spent
more
time
in
the
studio,
crafting
the
sound
of
the
album,
than
he
had
on
any
previous
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-ncvideo_29-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ncvideo-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Work
began
on
<i>The
Nylon
Curtain</i>
in
the
fall
of
1981
although
Joel's
work
on
the
album
was
temporary
delayed
when
he
was
involved
in
a
serious
motorcycle
accident
on
<a
href="/wiki/Long_Island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
Island">Long
Island</a>
on
April
15,
1982.
Still,
Joel
quickly
recovered
from
his
injuries,
and
the
album
only
ended
up
being
delayed
by
a
few
weeks.</p>








<p>In
1982,
he
embarked
on
a
brief
tour
in
support
of
the
album.
From
one
of
the
final
shows
of
the
tour,
Joel
made
his
first
video
special,
<i>Live
from
Long
Island,</i>
which
was
recorded
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nassau_Veterans_Memorial_Coliseum?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nassau
Veterans
Memorial
Coliseum">Nassau
Veterans
Memorial
Coliseum</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Uniondale,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uniondale,
New
York">Uniondale,
New
York</a>
on
December
30,
1982.
It
was
originally
broadcast
on
<a
href="/wiki/HBO?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="HBO">HBO</a>
in
1983
before
it
became
available
on
<a
href="/wiki/VHS?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VHS">VHS</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>The
Nylon
Curtain</i>
went
to
#7
on
the
charts,
partially
due
to
heavy
airplay
on
MTV
for
the
videos
to
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Allentown_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Allentown
(song)">Allentown</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pressure_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pressure
(Billy
Joel
song)">Pressure</a>&quot;.
&quot;Allentown&quot;
spent
six
weeks
at
a
peak
position
of
#17
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>,
making
it
one
of
the
most-played
radio
songs
of
1982,
pushing
it
into
1983's
year-end
Top
70,
and
making
it
the
most
successful
song
from
<i>The
Nylon
Curtain</i>
album,
besting
&quot;Pressure&quot;
which
peaked
at
#20
(where
it
resided
for
three
weeks)
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Goodnight_Saigon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goodnight
Saigon">Goodnight
Saigon</a>&quot;
which
reached
#56
on
U.S.
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Christie_Brinkley.2C_An_Innocent_Man.2C_and_The_Bridge">Christie
Brinkley,
<i>An
Innocent
Man</i>,
and
<i>The
Bridge</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Christie
Brinkley,
An
Innocent
Man,
and
The
Bridge">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:An_Innocent_Man_single.jpg"
target="_blank"

2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
