</div>
Billy
Joel
on
the
cover
of
the
&quot;An
Innocent
Man&quot;
EP,
1983.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Joel's
next
album
moved
away
from
the
serious
themes
of
<i>The
Nylon
Curtain</i>
and
struck
a
much
lighter
tone.
The
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/An_Innocent_Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="An
Innocent
Man">An
Innocent
Man</a></i>
was
Joel's
tribute
to
<a
href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rhythm
and
blues">R&amp;B</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Doo_wop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doo
wop"
class="mw-redirect">doo
wop</a>
music
of
the
1950s
and
1960s
and
resulted
in
Joel's
second
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>
#1
hit,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tell_Her_About_It?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tell
Her
About
It">Tell
Her
About
It</a>&quot;,
which
was
the
first
single
off
the
album
in
the
summer
of
1983.
The
album
itself
reached
#4
on
the
charts
and
#2
in
UK.
It
also
boasted
six
top-30
singles,
the
most
of
any
album
in
Joel's
catalog.
The
album
was
well
received
by
critics,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine">Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine</a>,
senior
editor
for
All
Music,
describing
Joel
as
being
&quot;in
top
form
as
a
craftsman
throughout
the
record,
effortlessly
spinning
out
infectious,
memorable
melodies
in
a
variety
of
styles.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>At
the
time
that
the
album
was
released,
<a
href="/wiki/WCBS-FM?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="WCBS-FM">WCBS-FM</a>
began
playing
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Uptown_Girl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uptown
Girl">Uptown
Girl</a>&quot;
both
in
regular
rotation
and
on
the
<i>Doo
Wop
Live</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
became
a
worldwide
hit
upon
its
release,
#3
in
the
U.S.
and
was
Joel's
sole
#1
in
the
United
Kingdom.
Also,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wilson_Pickett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wilson
Pickett">Wilson
Pickett</a>-inspired
song
&quot;Easy
Money&quot;
would
be
featured
in
the
1983
<a
href="/wiki/Easy_Money_(1983_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Easy
Money
(1983
film)">Rodney
Dangerfield
film</a>
of
the
same
name.<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December,
the
title
song,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/An_Innocent_Man_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="An
Innocent
Man
(song)">An
Innocent
Man</a>&quot;,
was
released
as
a
single
and
it
peaked
at
#10
in
the
U.S.
and
#8
in
the
UK,
early
in
1984.
That
March,
&quot;The
Longest
Time&quot;
was
released
as
a
single,
peaking
at
#14
on
the
Hot
100
and
#1
on
the
Adult
Contemporary
chart.
That
summer,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Leave_a_Tender_Moment_Alone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leave
a
Tender
Moment
Alone">Leave
a
Tender
Moment
Alone</a>&quot;
was
released
and
it
hit
#27
while
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Keeping_the_Faith_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keeping
the
Faith
(song)">Keeping
the
Faith</a>&quot;
peaked
at
#18
in
January
1985.
In
the
video
for
&quot;Keeping
the
Faith&quot;,
Christie
Brinkley
also
plays
the
&quot;redhead
girl
in
a
Chevrolet&quot;.
<i>An
Innocent
Man</i>
was
also
nominated
for
the
Album
of
the
Year
Grammy,
but
lost
to
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Jackson">Michael
Jackson</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thriller
(Michael
Jackson
album)">Thriller</a></i>.</p>








<p>Joel
participated
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/USA_For_Africa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="USA
For
Africa"
class="mw-redirect">USA
For
Africa</a>
<i><a
href="/wiki/We_Are_The_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Are
The
World"
class="mw-redirect">We
Are
The
World</a></i>
project
in
1985,
capping
off
a
series
of
successful
singles.</p>








<p>Following
the
success
of
<i>An
Innocent
Man</i>,
Joel
was
asked
about
releasing
an
album
of
his
most
successful
singles.
This
was
not
the
first
time
this
topic
had
come
up,
but
Joel
had
initially
considered
&quot;Greatest
Hits&quot;
albums
as
marking
the
end
of
one's
career.
This
time
he
agreed,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Billy_Joel_albums)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
Hits
(Billy
Joel
albums)">Greatest
Hits
Vol.
1
and
2</a></i>
was
released
as
a
four-sided
album
and
two-CD
set,
with
the
songs
in
the
order
in
which
they
were
released.
The
new
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You%27re_Only_Human_(Second_Wind)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You're
Only
Human
(Second
Wind)">You're
Only
Human
(Second
Wind)</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Night_Is_Still_Young_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Night
Is
Still
Young
(Billy
Joel
song)">The
Night
Is
Still
Young</a>&quot;
were
recorded
and
released
as
singles
to
support
the
album;
both
reached
the
top
40,
peaking
at
#9
and
#34,
respectively.</p>








<p><i>Greatest
Hits</i>
was
highly
successful
and
it
has
since
been
certified
<a
href="/wiki/Diamond_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diamond
album"
class="mw-redirect">double
diamond</a>
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>,
with
over
11.5&nbsp;million
copies
(23&nbsp;million
units)
sold.
To
date
it
is
tied
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_the_United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
albums
in
the
United
States">third-best-selling
album
in
American
music
history</a>,
according
to
the
RIAA.</p>








<p>Coinciding
with
the
<i>Greatest
Hits</i>
album
release,
Joel
released
a
two-volume
<i>Video
Album</i>
that
was
a
compilation
of
the
promotional
videos
he
had
recorded
from
1977
to
the
present
time.
Along
with
videos
for
the
new
singles
off
the
<i>Greatest
Hits</i>
album,
Joel
also
recorded
a
video
for
his
first
hit,
&quot;Piano
Man&quot;,
for
this
project.</p>








<p>Though
it
broke
into
the
top
ten,
Joel's
next
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Bridge_(Billy_Joel_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Bridge
(Billy
Joel
album)">The
Bridge</a></i>
(1986),
did
not
achieve
the
level
of
success
of
his
previous
albums,
but
it
yielded
the
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/A_Matter_of_Trust?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Matter
of
Trust">A
Matter
of
Trust</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Modern_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Modern
Woman">Modern
Woman</a>&quot;
from
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ruthless_People?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ruthless
People">Ruthless
People</a></i>,
a
dark
comedy
from
the
directors
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Airplane!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Airplane!">Airplane!</a></i>
(both
#10).
In
a
departure
from
his
&quot;piano
man&quot;
persona,
Joel
is
shown
in
the
video
playing
a
<a
href="/wiki/Les_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Les
Paul">Les
Paul</a>-autographed
Gibson
guitar.
The
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Is_the_Time_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Is
the
Time
(song)">This
is
the
Time</a>&quot;
also
charted,
peaking
at
#18.</p>








<p>On
November
18,
1986,
an
extended
version
of
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Big_Man_On_Mulberry_Street?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Man
On
Mulberry
Street"
class="mw-redirect">Big
Man
On
Mulberry
Street</a>&quot;
was
used
on
a
Season
3
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Moonlighting_(TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Moonlighting
(TV
series)">Moonlighting</a></i>.
The
episode
itself
was
also
titled
&quot;Big
Man
on
Mulberry
Street&quot;.</p>








<p><i>The
Bridge</i>
was
Joel's
last
album
to
carry
the
Family
Productions
logo,
after
which
he
severed
his
ties
with
Artie
Ripp.
Joel
has
also
stated
in
many
interviews,
most
recently
in
a
2008
interview
in
<i>Performing
Songwriter</i>
magazine,
that
he
does
not
think
<i>The
Bridge</i>
is
a
good
album.</p>








<p>Shortly
after
The
Bridge
tour
ended
in
late
1987,
Joel
completed
voice
work
on
Disney's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Oliver_%26_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oliver
&amp;
Company">Oliver
&amp;
Company</a>,</i>
released
in
1988,
a
loose
adaptation
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Charles
Dickens">Charles
Dickens</a>
novel
<i><a
href="/wiki/Oliver_Twist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oliver
Twist">Oliver
Twist</a>.</i>
Joel
brought
both
his
acting
and
musical
talents
to
the
film
as
Dodger.
For
the
film,
Joel
recorded
a
song
titled
&quot;Why
Should
I
Worry?&quot;
Critics
were
generally
positive
about
the
film,
pointing
to
Joel's
acting
as
one
of
its
highlights
despite
it
being
his
first
acting
job.
In
interviews,
Joel
explained
that
he
took
the
job
due
to
his
love
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Walt
Disney
Company">Disney</a>
cartoons
as
a
child.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Trip_to_the_Soviet_Union">Trip
to
the
Soviet
Union</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Trip
to
the
Soviet
Union">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
October
1986,
Joel
and
his
handlers
started
planning
a
trip
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Soviet_Union?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soviet
Union">Soviet
Union</a>.
He
became
one
of
the
first
American
rock
acts
to
play
there
since
the
<a
href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berlin
Wall">Berlin
Wall</a>
went
up,
a
fact
not
lost
on
history
buff
Joel.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
There
were
live
performances
at
indoor
arenas
in
Moscow,
<a
href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saint
Petersburg">Leningrad</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tbilisi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>.
Joel
and
his
family
(including
young
daughter
Alexa)
and
his
full
touring
band
made
the
trip
in
August
1987.
The
entourage
was
filmed
for
television
and
video
to
offset
the
cost
of
the
trip,
and
the
concerts
were
simulcast
on
radio
around
the
world.</p>








<p>Most
of
that
audience
took
a
long
while
to
warm
up
to
Joel's
energetic
show,
something
that
had
never
happened
in
other
countries
he
had
performed
in.
According
to
Joel,
each
time
the
fans
were
hit
with
the
bright
lights,
anybody
who
seemed
to
be
enjoying
themselves
froze.
In
addition,
people
who
were
&quot;overreacting&quot;
were
removed
by
security.<sup
id="cite_ref-SeattelWeekly_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SeattelWeekly-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
during
this
concert
that
Joel,
enraged
by
the
bright
lights,
flipped
his
piano
and
snapped
a
microphone
stand
while
continuing
to
sing
the
current
part
of
the
set.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
apologized
for
that
incident.</p>








<p>The
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kohuept?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kohuept"
class="mw-redirect">КОНЦЕРТ</a></i>
(Russian
for
&quot;Concert&quot;)
was
released
in
October
1987.
Singer
Peter
Hewlitt
was
brought
in
to
hit
the
high
notes
on
his
most
vocally
challenging
songs,
like
&quot;An
Innocent
Man&quot;.
Joel
also
did
versions
of
The
Beatles'
classic
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Back_in_the_U.S.S.R.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
in
the
U.S.S.R.">Back
in
the
U.S.S.R.</a>&quot;
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Dylan">Bob
Dylan</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Times_They_Are_a-Changin%27_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Times
They
Are
a-Changin'
(song)">The
Times
They
Are
a-Changin</a>&quot;.
It
has
been
estimated
that
Joel
lost
more
than
$1&nbsp;million
of
his
own
money
on
the
trip
and
concerts,
but
he
has
said
the
goodwill
he
was
shown
there
was
well
worth
it.<sup
id="cite_ref-unauthorized_20-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unauthorized-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Storm_Front_and_River_of_Dreams"><i>Storm
Front</i>
and
<i>River
of
Dreams</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Storm
Front
and
River
of
Dreams">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>The
release
of
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Storm_Front_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Storm
Front
(album)">Storm
Front</a></i>
coincided
with
major
changes
in
Joel's
career
and
inaugurated
a
period
of
serious
upheaval
in
his
business
affairs.
In
August
1989,
just
before
the
album
was
released,
Joel
dismissed
his
manager
(and
former
brother-in-law)
Frank
Weber
after
an
audit
revealed
major
discrepancies
in
Weber's
accounting.
Joel
subsequently
sued
Weber
for
$90
million,
claiming
fraud
and
breach
of
fiduciary
duty
and
in
January
1990
he
was
awarded
$2
million
in
a
partial
judgement
against
Weber;
in
April,
the
court
dismissed
a
$30
million
countersuit
filed
by
Weber.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
first
single
for
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We_Didn%27t_Start_the_Fire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Didn't
Start
the
Fire">We
Didn't
Start
the
Fire</a>&quot;,
was
released
in
September
1989
and
it
became
Joel's
third
and
most
recent
US
#1
hit,
spending
two
weeks
at
the
top;
it
was
also
Billboard's
second-last
#1
single
of
the
1980s.
<i>Storm
Front</i>
was
released
in
October,
and
it
eventually
became
Joel's
first
#1
album
since
<i>Glass
Houses</i>,
nine
years
earlier.
<i>Storm
Front</i>
was
Joel's
first
album
since
<i>Turnstiles</i>
to
be
recorded
without
Phil
Ramone
as
producer.
For
this
album,
he
wanted
a
new
sound,
and
worked
with
<a
href="/wiki/Mick_Jones_(Foreigner)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mick
Jones
(Foreigner)">Mick
Jones</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Foreigner_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foreigner
(band)">Foreigner</a>
fame.
Joel
is
also
credited
as
one
of
the
keyboard
players
on
Jones'
1988
self-titled
solo
album,
and
is
featured
in
the
official
video
for
Jones'
single
&quot;Just
Wanna
Hold&quot;;
Joel
can
be
seen
playing
the
piano
while
his
then-wife
Christie
Brinkley
joins
him
and
kisses
him.
Joel
also
revamped
his
backing
band,
dismissing
everyone
but
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Liberty_DeVitto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liberty
DeVitto">Liberty
DeVitto</a>,
guitarist
David
Brown,
and
saxophone
player
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Rivera?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Rivera">Mark
Rivera</a>,
and
bringing
in
new
faces,
including
multi-instrumentalist
<a
href="/wiki/Crystal_Taliefero?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crystal
Taliefero">Crystal
Taliefero</a>.</p>








<p><i>Storm
Front'</i>s
second
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Go_to_Extremes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Go
to
Extremes">I
Go
to
Extremes</a>&quot;
made
it
to
#6
in
early
1990.
The
album
was
also
notable
for
its
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Leningrad_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leningrad
(song)">Leningrad</a>&quot;,
written
after
Joel
met
a
clown
in
the
Soviet
city
of
that
name
during
his
tour
in
1987,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Downeaster_Alexa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Downeaster
Alexa">The
Downeaster
Alexa</a>&quot;,
written
to
underscore
the
plight
of
fishermen
on
Long
Island
who
are
barely
able
to
make
ends
meet.
Another
well-known
single
from
the
album
is
the
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/And_So_It_Goes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="And
So
It
Goes">And
So
It
Goes</a>&quot;
(#37
in
late
1990).
The
song
was
originally
written
in
1983,
around
the
time
Joel
was
writing
songs
for
<i>An
Innocent
Man</i>;
but
&quot;And
So
It
Goes&quot;
did
not
fit
that
album's
retro
theme,
so
it
was
held
back
until
<i>Storm
Front</i>.
Joel
said
in
a
1996
Masterclass
session
in
Pittsburgh
that
<i>Storm
Front</i>
was
a
turbulent
album
and
that
&quot;And
So
It
Goes&quot;,
as
the
last
song
on
the
album,
portrayed
the
calm
and
tranquility
that
often
follows
a
violent
thunderstorm.</p>








<p>In
the
summer
of
1992,
Joel
filed
another
$90
million
lawsuit
against
his
former
lawyer
Allen
Grubman,
alleging
a
wide
range
of
offenses
including
fraud,
breach
of
fiduciary
responsibility,
malpractice
and
breach
of
contract<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
but
the
case
was
eventually
settled
out
of
court
for
an
undisclosed
sum.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1992,
Joel
inducted
the
R&amp;B
duo
<a
href="/wiki/Sam_%26_Dave?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sam
&amp;
Dave">Sam
&amp;
Dave</a>
into
the
Rock
&amp;
Roll
Hall
of
Fame.
That
year,
Joel
also
started
work
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/River_of_Dreams?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="River
of
Dreams">River
of
Dreams</a></i>,
finishing
the
album
in
early
1993.
Its
cover
art
was
a
colorful
painting
by
<a
href="/wiki/Christie_Brinkley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christie
Brinkley">Christie
Brinkley</a>
that
was
a
series
of
scenes
from
each
of
the
songs
on
the
album.
The
eponymous
first
single
was
the
last
top
10
hit
Joel
has
penned
to
date,
reaching
#3
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100
&amp;
ranking
at
#21
on
<i>Billboard'</i>s
1993
year-end
Hot
100
chart.
In
addition
to
the
title
track,
the
album
includes
the
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_About_Soul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
About
Soul">All
About
Soul</a>&quot;
(with
<a
href="/wiki/Color_Me_Badd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Color
Me
Badd">Color
Me
Badd</a>
on
backing
vocals)
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lullabye_(Goodnight,_My_Angel)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lullabye
(Goodnight,
My
Angel)">Lullabye
(Goodnight,
My
Angel)</a>&quot;,
written
for
his
daughter,
<a
href="/wiki/Alexa_Ray_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alexa
Ray
Joel">Alexa</a>.
A
radio
remix
version
of
&quot;All
About
Soul&quot;
can
be
found
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Essential_Billy_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Essential
Billy
Joel">The
Essential
Billy
Joel</a></i>
(2001),
and
a
demo
version
appears
on
<i>My
Lives</i>
(2005).</p>








<p>The
song
&quot;The
Great
Wall
of
China&quot;
was
written
about
his
ex-manager
Frank
Weber
and
was
a
regular
in
the
setlist
for
Joel's
2006
tour.
&quot;2000
Years&quot;
was
prominent
in
the
millennium
concert
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>,
December
31,
1999,
and
&quot;Famous
Last
Words&quot;
closed
the
book
on
Joel's
pop
songwriting
for
more
than
a
decade.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1994.E2.80.932007">1994–2007</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
1994–2007">edit</a>]</span></h3>

tright">

Joel
performing
in
2007
in
Florida.

<p>On
August
25,
1994,
Joel
and
second
wife
<a
href="/wiki/Christie_Brinkley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christie
Brinkley">Christie
Brinkley</a>
divorced.</p>








<p>1997's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/To_Make_You_Feel_My_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="To
Make
You
Feel
My
Love"
class="mw-redirect">To
Make
You
Feel
My
Love</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hey_Girl_(Freddie_Scott_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hey
Girl
(Freddie
Scott
song)">Hey
Girl</a>&quot;
both
charted
from
Joel's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Billy_Joel_albums)?qsrc=3044#Greatest_Hits_Volume_III"
title="Greatest
Hits
(Billy
Joel
albums)">Greatest
Hits
Volume
III</a></i>
album.
Joel
wrote
and
recorded
the
song
&quot;Shameless&quot;
that
was
later
covered
by
<a
href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garth
Brooks">Garth
Brooks</a>
and
reached
number
1
on
Billboard's
country
charts.
Joel
performed
with
Brooks
during
his
<a
href="/wiki/Central_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Central
Park">Central
Park</a>
concert
in
1997
with
an
estimated
980,000
people
in
attendance,
the
largest
audience
to
attend
a
U.S.
concert.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(December
2010)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
To
add
onto
his
achievements
Joel
was
inducted
into
the
Rock
'n
Roll
Hall
of
Fame
in
1999.
Ray
Charles
made
the
induction
speech
and
mentioned
the
duet
Joel
wrote
for
the
two
of
them,
&quot;Baby
Grand&quot;
(a
track
on
Joel's
album
<i>The
Bridge</i>
released
in
1986).</p>








<p>On
December
31,
1999,
Joel
performed
at
New
York's
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>.
At
the
time,
Joel
said
that
it
would
be
his
last
tour
and
possibly
his
last
concert.
Two
of
his
performances
from
that
night,
<a
href="/wiki/We_Didn%27t_Start_the_Fire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Didn't
Start
the
Fire">We
Didn't
Start
the
Fire</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Scenes_from_an_Italian_Restaurant?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scenes
from
an
Italian
Restaurant">Scenes
from
an
Italian
Restaurant</a>
were
filmed
and
featured
that
night
as
part
of
ABC's
special
New
Year's
Y2K
coverage.
The
concert
(dubbed
The
Night
of
the
2000
Years)
ran
for
close
to
four
hours
and
was
later
released
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/2000_Years:_The_Millennium_Concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2000
Years:
The
Millennium
Concert">2000
Years:
The
Millennium
Concert</a></i>.</p>








<p>In
2001,
Joel
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fantasies_%26_Delusions?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fantasies
&amp;
Delusions">Fantasies
&amp;
Delusions</a></i>,
a
collection
of
classical
piano
pieces.
All
were
composed
by
Joel
and
performed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Richard_Joo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richard
Joo"
class="mw-redirect">Richard
Joo</a>.
Joel
often
uses
bits
of
these
songs
as
interludes
in
live
performances,
and
some
of
them
are
part
of
the
score
for
the
hit
show
<i><a
href="/wiki/Movin%27_Out_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Movin'
Out
(musical)">Movin'
Out</a></i>.
The
album
topped
the
classical
charts
at
#1.
Joel
performed
&quot;New
York
State
of
Mind&quot;
live
on
September
21,
2001,
as
part
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/America:_A_Tribute_to_Heroes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="America:
A
Tribute
to
Heroes">America:
A
Tribute
to
Heroes</a>
benefit
concert,
and
on
October
20,
2001,
along
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Miami_2017_(Seen_the_Lights_Go_Out_on_Broadway)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miami
2017
(Seen
the
Lights
Go
Out
on
Broadway)">Miami
2017
(Seen
the
Lights
Go
Out
on
Broadway)</a>&quot;,
at
<a
href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Concert
for
New
York
City">the
Concert
for
New
York
City</a>
in
Madison
Square
Garden.
That
night,
he
also
performed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Your_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Your
Song">Your
Song</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Elton_John?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elton
John">Elton
John</a>.</p>








<p>In
2003,
Joel
inducted
<a
href="/wiki/The_Righteous_Brothers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Righteous
Brothers">The
Righteous
Brothers</a>
into
the
Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame,
noting
that
his
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Until_the_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Until
the
Night">Until
the
Night</a>&quot;
from
the
album
<i>52nd
Street</i>
was
a
tribute
to
the
duo.</p>








<p>In
2005,
Columbia
released
a
box
set,
<i><a
href="/wiki/My_Lives?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Lives">My
Lives</a></i>,
which
is
largely
a
compilation
of
demos,
b-sides,
live/alternate
versions
and
even
a
few
Top
40
hits.
The
compilation
also
includes
the
<a
href="/wiki/Umixit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Umixit">Umixit</a>
software,
in
which
people
can
remix
&quot;Zanzibar&quot;
and
a
live
version
of
&quot;I
Go
to
Extremes&quot;
with
their
PC.
Also,
a
DVD
of
a
show
from
the
<i>River
of
Dreams</i>
tour
is
included.</p>








<p>On
January
7,
2006,
Joel
began
a
tour
across
the
United
States.
Having
not
written,
or
at
least
released,
any
new
songs
in
13
years,
he
featured
a
sampling
of
songs
from
throughout
his
career,
including
major
hits
as
well
as
obscure
tunes
like
&quot;Zanzibar&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_for_Leyna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
for
Leyna">All
for
Leyna</a>&quot;.
His
tour
included
an
unprecedented
12
sold-out
concerts
over
several
months
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>
in
New
York
City.
The
singer's
stint
of
12
shows
at
Madison
Square
Garden
broke
a
previous
record
set
by
New
Jersey
native
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Springsteen">Bruce
Springsteen</a>,
who
played
10
sold-out
shows
at
the
same
arena.
The
record
earned
Joel
the
first
retired
number
(12)
in
the
arena
owned
by
a
non-athlete.
This
honor
has
also
been
given
to
Joel
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Center_(Philadelphia)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wells
Fargo
Center
(Philadelphia)">Wells
Fargo
Center
(Philadelphia)</a>
(formerly
the
Wachovia
Center)
in
Philadelphia
where
a
banner
in
the
colors
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Philadelphia
Flyers">Philadelphia
Flyers</a>
is
hung
honoring
Joel's
46
Philadelphia
sold-out
shows.
He
also
had
a
banner
raised
in
his
honor
for
being
the
highest
grossing
act
in
the
history
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Times_Union_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Times
Union
Center">Times
Union
Center</a>
(formerly
the
Knickerbocker
Arena
and
Pepsi
Arena)
in
<a
href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Albany,
New
York">Albany,
New
York</a>.
This
honor
was
given
to
him
as
part
of
the
April
17,
2007,
show
he
did
there.
On
June
13,
2006,
Columbia
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/12_Gardens_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="12
Gardens
Live">12
Gardens
Live</a></i>,
a
double
album
containing
32
live
recordings
from
a
collection
of
the
12
different
shows
at
Madison
Square
Garden
during
Joel's
2006
tour.</p>








<p>Joel
visited
the
United
Kingdom
and
Ireland
for
the
first
time
in
many
years
as
part
of
the
European
leg
of
his
2006
tour.
On
July
31,
2006,
he
performed
a
free
concert
in
Rome,
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Colosseum?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a>
as
the
backdrop.
Organizers
estimated
500,000
people
turned
out
for
the
concert,
which
was
opened
by
<a
href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bryan
Adams">Bryan
Adams</a>.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(December
2010)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>








<p>Joel
toured
South
Africa,
Australia,
Japan,
and
Hawaii
in
late
2006,
and
subsequently
toured
the
Southeastern
United
States
in
February
and
March
2007
before
hitting
the
Midwest
in
the
spring
of
2007.
On
January
3
of
that
year,
news
was
leaked
to
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/New_York_Post?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
Post">New
York
Post</a></i>
that
Billy
had
recorded
a
new
song
with
lyrics—this
being
the
first
new
song
with
lyrics
he'd
written
in
almost
14
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song,
titled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_My_Life_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
My
Life
(Billy
Joel
song)">All
My
Life</a>&quot;,
was
Joel's
newest
single
(with
second
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You%27re_My_Home?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You're
My
Home">You're
My
Home</a>&quot;,
live
from
Madison
Square
Garden
2006
tour)
and
was
released
into
stores
on
February
27,
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
February
4,
Joel
sang
the
national
anthem
for
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLI?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Super
Bowl
XLI">Super
Bowl
XLI</a>,
becoming
the
first
to
sing
the
national
anthem
twice
at
a
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Super
Bowl">Super
Bowl</a>.
and
on
April
17,
2007,
Joel
was
honored
in
Albany,
New
York,
for
his
ninth
concert
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Times_Union_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Times
Union
Center">Times
Union
Center</a>.
He
is
now
holding
the
highest
box
office
attendance
of
any
artist
to
play
at
the
arena.
A
banner
was
raised
in
his
honor
marking
this
achievement.</p>








<p>On
December
1,
2007,
Joel
premiered
his
new
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Christmas_in_Fallujah?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christmas
in
Fallujah">Christmas
in
Fallujah</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
was
performed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Cass_Dillon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cass
Dillon">Cass
Dillon</a>,
a
new
Long
Island
based
musician,
as
Joel
felt
it
should
be
sung
by
someone
in
a
soldier's
age
range
(though
he
himself
has
played
the
song
occasionally
in
concert.)
The
track
was
dedicated
to
servicemen
based
in
Iraq.
Joel
wrote
it
in
September
2007
after
reading
numerous
letters
sent
to
him
from
American
soldiers
in
Iraq.
&quot;Christmas
in
Fallujah&quot;
is
only
the
second
pop/rock
song
released
by
Joel
since
1993's
<i>River
of
Dreams</i>.
Proceeds
from
the
song
benefitted
the
Homes
For
Our
Troops
foundation.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2008.E2.80.93present">2008–present</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
2008–present">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>On
January
26,
2008,
Joel
performed
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Orchestra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Philadelphia
Orchestra">Philadelphia
Orchestra</a>
celebrating
the
151st
anniversary
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Music_(Philadelphia)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Music
(Philadelphia)">Academy
of
Music</a>.
Joel
premiered
his
new
classical
piece
titled,
&quot;Waltz
No.
2
(Steinway
Hall)&quot;
arranged
by
<a
href="/wiki/Brad_Ellis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brad
Ellis">Brad
Ellis</a>.
He
also
played
many
of
his
less
well-known
pieces,
with
full
orchestral
backing
arranged
by
Mr.
Ellis,
including
the
rarely
performed
<i>Nylon
Curtain</i>
songs
&quot;Scandinavian
Skies&quot;
and
&quot;Where's
the
Orchestra?&quot;.</p>








<p>On
March
10,
2008,
Joel
inducted
his
friend
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mellencamp?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mellencamp">John
Mellencamp</a>
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
a
ceremony
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Waldorf_Astoria_Hotel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Waldorf
Astoria
Hotel"
class="mw-redirect">Waldorf
Astoria
Hotel</a>
in
New
York
City.</p>








<p>Joel's
staying
power
as
a
touring
act
continues
to
the
present
day.
He
sold
out
10
concerts
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mohegan_Sun_Casino?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mohegan
Sun
Casino"
class="mw-redirect">Mohegan
Sun
Casino</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Uncasville,_Connecticut?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uncasville,
Connecticut">Uncasville,
Connecticut</a>
from
May
to
July
2008.
The
casino
honored
him
with
a
banner
displaying
his
name
and
the
number
10
to
hang
in
the
arena.
On
June
19,
2008,
he
played
a
concert
at
the
grand
re-opening
of
<a
href="/wiki/Caesars_Windsor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Caesars
Windsor">Caesars
Windsor</a>
(formerly
Casino
Windsor)
in
<a
href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Windsor,
Ontario">Windsor,
Ontario</a>,
Canada
to
an
invite-only
crowd
for
Casino
VIPs.
His
mood
was
light,
and
joke-filled,
even
introducing
himself
as
&quot;Billy
Joel's
dad&quot;
and
stating
&quot;you
guys
overpaid
to
see
a
fat
bald
guy&quot;.
He
also
admitted
that
Canadian
folk-pop
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Gordon_Lightfoot?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gordon
Lightfoot">Gordon
Lightfoot</a>
was
the
musical
inspiration
for
&quot;She's
Always
A
Woman&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
July
16,
2008,
and
July
18,
2008,
Joel
played
the
final
concerts
at
<a
href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shea
Stadium">Shea
Stadium</a>
before
its
demolition.
His
guests
included
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Bennett">Tony
Bennett</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Don_Henley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don
Henley">Don
Henley</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mayer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mayer">John
Mayer</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mellencamp?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mellencamp">John
Mellencamp</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Daltrey">Roger
Daltrey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garth
Brooks">Garth
Brooks</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
McCartney">Paul
McCartney</a>.
The
concerts
were
featured
in
the
2010
documentary
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Last_Play_at_Shea?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Play
at
Shea"
class="mw-redirect">Last
Play
at
Shea</a></i>.
The
film
was
released
on
DVD
on
February
8,
2011.
The
CD
and
DVD
of
the
show,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_at_Shea_Stadium:_The_Concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
at
Shea
Stadium:
The
Concert">Live
at
Shea
Stadium</a></i>
were
released
on
March
8,
2011.</p>








<p>On
December
11,
2008,
Joel
recorded
his
own
rendition
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Christmas_in_Fallujah?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christmas
in
Fallujah">Christmas
in
Fallujah</a>&quot;
during
a
concert
at
<a
href="/wiki/Acer_Arena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Acer
Arena"
class="mw-redirect">Acer
Arena</a>
in
Sydney
and
released
it
as
a
live
single
in
Australia
only.
It
is
the
only
official
release
of
Joel
performing
&quot;Christmas
in
Fallujah&quot;,
as
Cass
Dillon
sang
on
the
2007
studio
recording
and
the
handful
of
times
the
song
was
played
live
in
2007.
Joel
sang
the
song
throughout
his
December
2008
tour
of
Australia.</p>








<p>On
May
19,
2009,
Joel's
former
drummer,
<a
href="/wiki/Liberty_DeVitto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liberty
DeVitto">Liberty
DeVitto</a>,
filed
a
lawsuit
in
NYC
claiming
Joel
and
Sony
Music
owed
DeVitto
over
10
years
of
royalty
payments.
DeVitto
had
never
been
given
songwriting
or
arranging
credit
on
any
of
Joel's
songs,
but
he
claimed
that
he
helped
arrange
some
of
them,
including
&quot;Only
the
Good
Die
Young&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Joel.27s_Former_Drummer_Sues_for_Payments_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Joel.27s_Former_Drummer_Sues_for_Payments-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
April
2010,
it
was
announced
that
Joel
and
DeVitto
amicably
resolved
the
lawsuit.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
December
12,
2012,
Joel
played
in
<a
href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="12-12-12:
The
Concert
for
Sandy
Relief">12-12-12:
The
Concert
for
Sandy
Relief</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>.
The
concert
was
for
all
the
victims
of
<a
href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hurricane
Sandy">Hurricane
Sandy</a>.
He
changed
the
lyrics
to
<a
href="/wiki/Miami_2017_(Seen_the_Lights_Go_Out_on_Broadway)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miami
2017
(Seen
the
Lights
Go
Out
on
Broadway)">Miami
2017</a>
to
make
it
relate
to
all
the
damage
caused
by
Sandy.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2011_re-releases">2011
re-releases</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
2011
re-releases">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>2011
marked
the
40th
anniversary
of
the
release
of
Joel's
first
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cold_Spring_Harbor_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cold
Spring
Harbor
(album)">Cold
Spring
Harbor</a>.</i>
According
to
Joel's
official
website,
to
commemorate
this
anniversary,
Columbia/Legacy
Recordings
originally
planned
&quot;to
celebrate
the
occasion
with
a
definitive
reissue
project
of
newly
restored
and
expanded
Legacy
editions
of
the
complete
Billy
Joel
catalog,
newly
curated
collections
of
rarities
from
the
vaults,
previously
unavailable
studio
tracks
and
live
performances,
home
video
releases
and
more&quot;,
although
this
never
fully
came
to
fruition.<sup
id="cite_ref-Billy_Joel.27s_Website_48-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Billy_Joel.27s_Website-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Piano_Man_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piano
Man
(album)">Piano
Man</a></i>
was
re-released
in
a
2-disc
Legacy
edition
in
November
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-Billy_Joel.27s_Website_48-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Billy_Joel.27s_Website-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Face-to-Face_tours">Face-to-Face
tours</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"
title="Edit
section:
Face-to-Face
tours">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Beginning
in
1994,
Joel
toured
extensively
with
<a
href="/wiki/Elton_John?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elton
John">Elton
John</a>
on
a
series
of
&quot;Face
to
Face&quot;
tours,
making
them
the
longest
running
and
most
successful
concert
tandem
in
pop
music
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
these
shows,
the
two
have
played
their
own
songs,
each
other's
songs
and
performed
duets.
They
grossed
over
US
$46&nbsp;million
in
just
24
dates
in
their
sold
out<sup
id="cite_ref-livedaily_50-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-livedaily-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
2003
tour.
Joel
and
John
resumed
the
Face
to
Face
tour
in
March
2009<sup
id="cite_ref-livedaily_50-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-livedaily-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
it
ended
again,
at
least
for
the
time
being,
in
March
2010
in
<a
href="/wiki/Albany,_NY?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Albany,
NY"
class="mw-redirect">Albany,
NY</a>,
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Times_Union_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Times
Union
Center">Times
Union
Center</a>.
In
February
2010,
Joel
denied
rumors
in
the
trade
press
that
he
canceled
a
summer
2010
leg
of
the
tour,
claiming
there
were
never
any
dates
booked
and
that
he
intended
to
take
the
year
off.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joel
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
magazine:
&quot;We’ll
probably
pick
it
up
again.
It’s
always
fun
playing
with
him.&quot;
However,
in
March
2012
he
told
an
audience
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/University_of_Florida?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="University
of
Florida">University
of
Florida</a>
that
the
Face
to
Face
shows
“got
to
be
a
little
confining”
because
Elton
John
insisted
that
they
keep
playing
the
same
sets.
“I
don't
think
we'll
do
it
anymore,”
Joel
said.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2013.2F2014_Concerts">2013/2014
Concerts</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"
title="Edit
section:
2013/2014
Concerts">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
May
2013
it
was
announced
that
Joel
will
be
holding
his
first
ever
indoor
Irish
concert
at
the
O2
in
Dublin
on
November
1.
He
subsequently
announced
his
return
to
the
UK
for
the
first
time
in
seven
years
to
perform
three
dates
in
October
and
November.
Joel
will
play
two
arena
dates
in
Manchester
and
Birmingham
plus
a
very
special
-
more
intimate
-
show
at
London’s
Hammersmith
Apollo.
In
October,
Billy
Joel
held
a
surprise
concert
on
Long
Island
at
The
Paramount
(Huntington,
NY)
to
benefit
Long
Island
Cares.
The
venue
holds
a
capacity
of
1,555
and
sold
out
in
5
minutes.
Joel
headlined
a
solo
arena
concert
in
New
York
City
for
the
first
time
since
2006
when
he
performed
at
Barclays
Center
in
Brooklyn
on
December
31,
2013.
In
2014,
Joel
will
perform
21
concerts
(in
addition
to
his
Madison
Square
Garden
residency)
from
January
7
to
August
2
in
various
cities
around
the
United
States
and
Canada.
Billy
Joel
also
performed
at
the
Palace
of
Auburn
Hills
in
(Detroit)
Michigan.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="MSG_Residency">MSG
Residency</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
MSG
Residency">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>On
December
3,
2013,
it
was
announced
that
Joel
would
become
a
franchise
of
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>,
playing
one
concert
a
month
indefinitely,
starting
with
a
date
on
January
27,
2014.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Other_ventures">Other
ventures</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"
title="Edit
section:
Other
ventures">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Joel
voiced
one
of
the
main
characters
in
the
1988
Disney
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Oliver_%26_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oliver
&amp;
Company">Oliver
&amp;
Company</a></i>.
It
is
the
only
time
Joel
ever
took
on
an
acting
role
in
a
movie.</p>








<p>In
1996,
Joel
merged
his
long-held
love
of
boating<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
with
his
desire
for
a
second
career.
He
formed,
with
Long
Island
boating
businessman
Peter
Needham,
the
Long
Island
Boat
Company.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
November
2010,
Joel
opened
a
shop
on
Oyster
Bay,
Long
Island
to
manufacture
custom-made,
retro-styled
motorcycles
and
accessories.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2011,
Joel
announced
that
he
was
releasing
an
autobiography
that
he
had
written
with
Fred
Schruers,
titled
<i>The
Book
of
Joel:
A
Memoir</i>.
The
book
was
originally
going
to
be
released
in
June
2011,
but
in
March
2011
Joel
decided
against
publishing
the
book
and
officially
cancelled
his
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/HarperCollins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="HarperCollins">HarperCollins</a>.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
noted,
&quot;HarperCollins
acquired
the
book
project
for
$3
million
in
2008.
[However,]
Joel
is
expected
to
return
his
advance
on
that
sum
to
the
publisher.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>,
&quot;the
HarperCollins
book
was
billed
as
an
'emotional
ride'
that
would
detail
the
music
legend's
failed
marriage
to
<a
href="/wiki/Christie_Brinkley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christie
Brinkley">Christie
Brinkley</a>,
as
well
as
his
battles
with
substance
abuse.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
explaining
his
decision
to
cancel
the
book's
release,
Joel
stated,
&quot;It
took
working
on
writing
a
book
to
make
me
realize
that
I'm
not
all
that
interested
in
talking
about
the
past,
and
that
the
best
expression
of
my
life
and
its
ups
and
downs
has
been
and
remains
my
music.&quot;
<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
January
2014,
Joel
appeared
as
himself
in
<a
href="/wiki/Adam_Scott_(actor)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adam
Scott
(actor)">Adam
Scott</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Adult_Swim?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adult
Swim">Adult
Swim</a>
series:
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Greatest_Event_in_Television_History?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Greatest
Event
in
Television
History">The
Greatest
Event
in
Television
History</a></i>,
singing
his
song
&quot;My
Life&quot;
for
a
recreation
of
the
opening
theme
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bosom_Buddies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bosom
Buddies">Bosom
Buddies</a></i>.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_life">Personal
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Marriages.2C_relationships.2C_and_family">Marriages,
relationships,
and
family</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19"
title="Edit
section:
Marriages,
relationships,
and
family">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Joel
married
his
business
manager,
Elizabeth
Weber
Small,
on
September
5,
1973.
She
was
the
former
wife
of
his
music
partner,
Jon
Small,
in
the
short-lived
duo
<a
href="/wiki/Attila_(rock_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Attila
(rock
band)">Attila</a>.
Joel
and
Elizabeth
divorced
on
July
20,
1982.</p>








<p>Joel
mentioned
in
a
television
interview
on
the
UK's
<a
href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Channel
5
(UK)">Five</a>
that
he
had
dated
<a
href="/wiki/Elle_Macpherson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elle
Macpherson">Elle
Macpherson</a>
in
the
1980s
prior
to
his
marriage
to
<a
href="/wiki/Christie_Brinkley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christie
Brinkley">Christie
Brinkley</a>.
Joel
has
also
said
that
the
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Night_(Billy_Joel_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Night
(Billy
Joel
song)">This
Night</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/And_So_It_Goes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="And
So
It
Goes">And
So
It
Goes</a>&quot;
were
written
about
his
relationship
with
Macpherson.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ch5Interview_59-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ch5Interview-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Joel's

<p>Joel
married
Christie
Brinkley
on
March
23,
1985.
Their
daughter,
<a
href="/wiki/Alexa_Ray_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alexa
Ray
Joel">Alexa
Ray
Joel</a>,
was
born
December
29,
1985.<sup
id="cite_ref-atl1_60-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-atl1-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
Alexa
was
given
the
middle
name
of
Ray
after
<a
href="/wiki/Ray_Charles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ray
Charles">Ray
Charles</a>,
one
of
Joel's
musical
idols.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joel
and
Brinkley
divorced
on
August
25,
1994;
the
couple
remain
friendly.</p>








<p>On
October
2,
2004,
Joel
married
23-year-old
<a
href="/wiki/Katie_Lee_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Katie
Lee
Joel"
class="mw-redirect">Katie
Lee</a>.
At
the
time
of
the
wedding,
Joel
was
55.
Joel's
daughter,
Alexa
Ray,
then
18,
served
as
<a
href="/wiki/Maid-of-honor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maid-of-honor"
class="mw-redirect">maid-of-honor</a>.
Joel's
second
wife,
Christie
Brinkley,
attended
the
union
and
gave
the
couple
her
blessing.
Lee
works
as
a
restaurant
correspondent
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/PBS?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PBS">PBS</a>
show,
<i>George
Hirsch:
Living
it
Up!</i>.
In
2006,
Katie
Lee
hosted
<a
href="/wiki/Bravo_(US_TV_network)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bravo
(US
TV
network)"
class="mw-redirect">Bravo</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Top_Chef?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
Chef">Top
Chef</a></i>.
She
did
not
return
for
a
second
season,
instead
going
on
tour
with
her
husband.
She
then
began
writing
a
weekly
column
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Hamptons_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hamptons
(magazine)">Hamptons</a></i>
magazine,
and
became
a
field
correspondent
for
the
entertainment
television
show
<a
href="/wiki/Extra_(TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extra
(TV
series)"
class="mw-redirect"><i>Extra</i></a>.
On
June
17,
2009,
both
confirmed
that
they
had
split
after
five
years
of
marriage.<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_troubles">Personal
troubles</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
troubles">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Joel
battled
<a
href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Major
depressive
disorder">depression</a>
for
many
years.
In
1970,
a
career
downturn
and
personal
problems
aggravated
his
condition.
He
left
a
suicide
note
(which
inspired
the
lyrics
to
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tomorrow_is_Today_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tomorrow
is
Today
(song)"
class="mw-redirect">Tomorrow
Is
Today</a>&quot;)
and
attempted
to
commit
suicide
by
drinking
furniture
polish,
saying
later,
&quot;I
drank
furniture
polish.
It
looked
tastier
than
bleach.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-unauthorized_20-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unauthorized-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
drummer
assistant,
Jon
Small,
rushed
him
to
the
hospital.
Joel
checked
into
Meadowbrook
Hospital,
where
he
was
put
on
<a
href="/wiki/Suicide_watch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suicide
watch">suicide
watch</a>
and
received
treatment
for
depression.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joel
later
recorded
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You%27re_Only_Human_(Second_Wind)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You're
Only
Human
(Second
Wind)">You're
Only
Human
(Second
Wind)</a>&quot;
as
a
message
to
help
prevent
teen
suicide.</p>








<p>In
2002,
Joel
entered
Silver
Hill
Hospital,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Substance_abuse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Substance
abuse">substance
abuse</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Psychiatric?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Psychiatric"
class="mw-redirect">psychiatric</a>
center
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_Canaan,_Connecticut?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Canaan,
Connecticut">New
Canaan,
Connecticut</a>.
In
March
2005,
he
checked
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Betty_Ford_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Betty
Ford
Center">Betty
Ford
Center</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
where
he
spent
30
days
for
the
treatment
of
alcohol-related
problems.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Politics">Politics</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21"
title="Edit
section:
Politics">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Although
Joel
has
donated
money
to
<a
href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Democratic
Party
(United
States)">Democratic</a>
candidates
running
for
office,<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
he
has
never
publicly
affiliated
himself
with
the
Democratic
Party.
Although
he
isn't
known
for
publicly
endorsing
political
candidates,
he
did
play
a
benefit
with
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Springsteen">Bruce
Springsteen</a>
to
raise
money
for
<a
href="/wiki/Barack_Obama?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barack
Obama">Barack
Obama</a>'s
presidential
campaign
in
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
has
also
played
at
benefit
concerts
that
have
helped
raise
funds
for
political
causes.
However,
Joel
has
said
about
musicians
endorsing
political
candidates,
&quot;People
who
pay
for
your
tickets,
I
don't
think
they
want
to
hear
who
you're
going
to
vote
for
and
how
you
think
they
should
vote.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Religion">Religion</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Billy_Joel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22"
title="Edit
section:
Religion">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Joel
was
born
to
non-observant
<a
href="/wiki/Jews?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jews">Jewish</a>
parents
and
considers
himself
a
<a
href="/wiki/Cultural_Judaism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cultural
Judaism">cultural
Jew</a>.
He
stated
in
2001:</p>








<table
class="cquote"
style="margin:auto;
border-collapse:
collapse;
border:
none;
background-color:
transparent;
width:
auto;">









<tbody>









<tr>











<td
width="20"
valign="top"
style="border:none;
color:#B2B7F2;font-size:35px;font-family:
'Times
New
Roman',
serif;
font-weight:
bold;
text-align:
left;
padding:
10px
10px;">“</td>











<td
valign="top"
style="border:
none;
padding:
4px
10px;">My
parents
were
both
from
Jewish
families.
I
was
not
brought
up
Jewish
in
any
religious
way.
My
circumcision
was
as
Jewish
as
they
got.
I
used
to
go
to
Roman
Catholic
church
with
my
friends,
and
when
I
was
11,
I
got
baptized
in
a
Church
of
Christ
in
Hicksville.
I’m
a
cultural
Jew.
I
like
the
Lower
East
Side
humor,
the
food.
I
think
the
Yiddish
language
is
terrifically
expressive.
Does
that
make
me
a
complete
Jew
or
a
partial
Jew?
I’m
not
really
sure.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></td>











<td
width="20"
valign="bottom"
style="border:
none;
color:
#B2B7F2;
font-size:
35px;
font-family:
'Times
New
Roman',
serif;
font-weight:
bold;
text-align:
right;
padding:
10px
10px;">”</td>










</tr>









</tbody>







</table>








<p>During
a
2010
interview
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Howard_Stern_Show?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Howard
Stern
Show">The
Howard
Stern
Show</a></i>,
Joel
reiterated
his
<a
href="/wiki/Atheism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Atheism">atheism</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Billy

an

Doctorate
of
Fine
Arts
from











<a
href="/wiki/Syracuse_University?qsrc=3044"

<p>Joel
graduated
well
after
his
high
school
peers
because
of
a
missed
English
exam.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
high
school
diploma
was
finally
awarded
by
the
school
board
25
years
later.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joel
has
been
presented
with
multiple
<a
href="/wiki/Honorary_degree?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honorary
degree">honorary
doctorates</a>:</p>








<ul>









<li>Doctor
of
Humane
Letters
from
<a
href="/wiki/Fairfield_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fairfield
University">Fairfield
University</a>
(1991)</li>









<li>Doctor
of
Music
from
<a
href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berklee
College
of
Music">Berklee
College
of
Music</a>
(1993)</li>









<li>Doctor
of
Humane
Letters
from
<a
href="/wiki/Hofstra_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hofstra
University">Hofstra
University</a>
(1997)</li>









<li>Doctor
of
Music
from
<a
href="/wiki/Southampton_College?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Southampton
College"
class="mw-redirect">Southampton
College</a>
(2000)</li>









<li>Doctor
of
Fine
Arts
from
<a
href="/wiki/Syracuse_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Syracuse

University</a>
(2006)<sup

<li>Doctor
of

Arts

<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manhattan

School
of

(2008)</li>








</ul>








<p>In
1986,
Joel
was
on
the
site
selection
committee
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
board.
Seven
members
of
the
committee
voted
for
the
Hall
to
be
located
in
<a
href="/wiki/San_Francisco?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Francisco">San
Francisco</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="California">California</a>,
and
seven
voted
for
<a
href="/wiki/Cleveland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ohio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ohio">Ohio</a>;
this
tie
was
broken
when
Billy
Joel
voted
for
Cleveland.
Joel
was
inducted
into
the
Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame
in
Cleveland
in
1999
by
one
of
his
chief
musical
influences,
<a
href="/wiki/Ray_Charles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ray
Charles">Ray
Charles</a>.</p>








<p>Joel
was
also
named
<a
href="/wiki/MusiCares_Person_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MusiCares
Person
of
the
Year">MusiCares
Person
of
the
Year</a>
for
2002,<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
an
award
given
each
year
at
the
same
time
as
the
Grammy
Awards.
At
the
dinner
honoring
Joel,
various
artists
performed
versions
of
his
songs
including
<a
href="/wiki/Nelly_Furtado?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nelly
Furtado">Nelly
Furtado</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stevie
Wonder">Stevie
Wonder</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jon_Bon_Jovi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Bon
Jovi">Jon
Bon
Jovi</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Diana_Krall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diana
Krall">Diana
Krall</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rob_Thomas_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rob
Thomas
(musician)">Rob
Thomas</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Natalie_Cole?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Natalie
Cole">Natalie
Cole</a>.
Joel
has
won
five
non-honorary
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Album
of
the
Year">Album
of
the
Year</a>,
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/52nd_Street_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="52nd
Street
(album)">52nd
Street</a></i>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
